    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10893360339882133899">The long siege of Troy, the battles fought over it, and the city's eventual capitulation and incineration are events which have often been retold since their first recitation by Homer. Seldom, however, will they have been narrated with such close attention to the minute particulars of battle, to its reek and terror and pain, as in this startling account by Daniel Kelly. Ke</span>
  <span id="freeText10893360339882133899" style="display:none">The long siege of Troy, the battles fought over it, and the city's eventual capitulation and incineration are events which have often been retold since their first recitation by Homer. Seldom, however, will they have been narrated with such close attention to the minute particulars of battle, to its reek and terror and pain, as in this startling account by Daniel Kelly. Kelly looks minutely at every detail of archaic combat, as well as at the lives and feelings shaped by it. His Troy is not only a scene of shining glory, but also a grimy struggle for survival and mastery. And he introduces surprising questions: what if not everything in the Trojan war came to pass just as Homer tells us? What if the future of the Roman empire were hidden in the burning ashes of Troy's - and not in the way we might expect?</span>
  <a data-text-id="10893360339882133899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2861476383" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2861476383" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2861476383?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2861476383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9371587411519725430">Inside the Trojan horse and other secrets<br/><br/>Irish author Daniel Kelly received his training as a chef from Tourism College, Killybegs and has pursued his passion for history by creating this fascinating book about Troy, offering fresh insights into the Trojan War and the famous heroes of Greek literature.<br/><br/>Daniel’s writing style is conducive to penetrating fact from fiction, as his opening Prologue suggests – ‘Under the warm morning sun one man stood alone in a circle, surrounded by enemies bent on d</span>
  <span id="freeText9371587411519725430" style="display:none">Inside the Trojan horse and other secrets<br /><br />Irish author Daniel Kelly received his training as a chef from Tourism College, Killybegs and has pursued his passion for history by creating this fascinating book about Troy, offering fresh insights into the Trojan War and the famous heroes of Greek literature.<br /><br />Daniel’s writing style is conducive to penetrating fact from fiction, as his opening Prologue suggests – ‘Under the warm morning sun one man stood alone in a circle, surrounded by enemies bent on destroying his city. His circle of twenty, his personal bodyguard, unmoving; facing outwards with heavy shields, spears in hand and sheathed swords, they seemed a fairly flimsy barrier around the ring. Resplendent in the heavy bronze armour of a prince of his city, Hector looked out across the sea of faces, all of whom wanted him dead. He didn’t fear them, however; he knew that none dared approach, though unafraid of him: any of them would die happy if they were the one to take his life, knowing that their name would live down through the ages. A trumpet blasted further down the beach, and at this he did feel fear; it echoed in his head as his own death toll, because this was the day he would die. The man who held his enemies at bay was approaching. Achilles, his childhood friend, his training companion, had claimed the right to his life that very morning as revenge for the death of his little brother: a right Hector could not deny. Watching the approach of the black-armoured Myrmidons leading Achilles on his chariot, Hector recalled every training bout he had ever fought against Achilles, and vainly tried to remember some slip, some weakness shown. Achilles was a legend come to life; he never made the same mistake twice, and remembered every trick. At fourteen, he had bested his tutors.’<br /><br />This book explores the historic time surround the Trojan war with such definitive skill that all lovers of ancient history will discover a new light on the mysteries surrounding mythology and history. Daniel’s detailed accounts of battles and skirmishes and relationships are so raw and vivid that the legends come to life as never before. Hopefully this fine writer will continue his explorations of history with further books of the quality of this one. Highly recommended<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9371587411519725430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3278846396" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3278846396" />
    <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance"><img alt="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600345081p2/53419883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3278846396?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance">Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3278846396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8217509092435498799"><b>There is something to be said about writing a period piece that feels so organic in the delivery as The Fall of The Phoenix does.</b> From the first page to the last, it summons the reader to be part of the atmospheric and antiquated time of the Trojan War, seemingly effortlessly allured, filled with valor, honor, and heart. <br/> <br/>At center stage are the familiar players like Hector, Achilles, Agamemnon, Odysseus, Ajax, Priam, and Diomedes but also a few other key figures important in the turn of events </span>
  <span id="freeText8217509092435498799" style="display:none"><b>There is something to be said about writing a period piece that feels so organic in the delivery as The Fall of The Phoenix does.</b> From the first page to the last, it summons the reader to be part of the atmospheric and antiquated time of the Trojan War, seemingly effortlessly allured, filled with valor, honor, and heart. <br /> <br />At center stage are the familiar players like Hector, Achilles, Agamemnon, Odysseus, Ajax, Priam, and Diomedes but also a few other key figures important in the turn of events in this novel as well as Homer himself!<br /><br />The story begins near the end of the long 10-year Trojan War that has left the citizens of Troy marginally starving and depleted of their resources. Greek troops have made camp on the beach all these years while fresh supplies have come in from the homeland in steady intervals to their aid and nourishment; but they are weary and ready to go home - it has been a long 10 years. Word has it that northern horse tribes are threatening the homes and families of the Greek citizens and the Trojan War has to come to an end once and for all so the soldiers can go home.<br /><br /><b>HECTOR KNOWS HE WILL DIE TODAY.</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>Under the warm morning sun, one man stood alone in a circle, surrounded by enemies bent on destroying his city. His circle of twenty, his personal bodyguard, unmoving; facing outwards with heavy shields, spears in hand and sheathed swords, hey seemed a fairly flimsy barrier around the ring.<br /> Resplendent in the heavy bronze armour of a prince of his city, Hector looked out across the sea of faces, all of whom wanted him dead. He didn't fear them, however; he knew that none dared approach, though unafraid of him: any of them would die happy if they were the on to take his life, knowing that their name would live down through the ages. A trumped blasted further down the beach, and at this, he did feel fear; it echoed in his head as his won death toll, because this was the day he would die."</b>
</i><br /><br />In the breath of premonition, Hector falls while an arrow misses its mark. Achilles drags his opponent into the gates of Troy while he finds the archer of the untimely arrow; a young Diomedes all eager to take his father's place in the phalanx but too young to join.<br />Achilles takes the young Trojan to be his servant boy back to his camp and teaches him a lesson or two. He provides Diomedes with lavish foods he hasn’t had in years and makes him partake in the preparations for the funeral for his fallen brother Patroclus. As Achilles guides the lad in sparring lessons and moments of heart to heart conversations, one might think he is preparing him for something still to come. <br /><br /><b>BUT THE TROJANS ARE READY FOR A SURPRISE ATTACK AND A VICTORY FOR THEIR MORALE.</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>"But today I tell you that Troy is not dead because of the fall of one man, because Troy is much greater than any one man! Troy is the spirit, the embodiment, of all men who want to be free of the yoke of Mycenaean oppression. I tell you today that, as long as one man is left to defend the phoenix the Troy lives."</b>
</i><br /><br />As the Trojans relish in their zealot roars, the Greeks prepare new plans of their own in the form of an offering so they can go back home to Greece marking one last strike.<br /><br />This is the part of the book where Kelly's tools of deception make the grand entrance to the story that will flip what you know of the original in a well thought out and masterfully choreographed inception of twists and turns into a new work of intrigue. Most ingeniously, this new narrative welcomes a different mythology to the plot that furthers a provoking addition of characters and events, offering the possibility of a "New" Iliad by Homer, who makes his appearance at the most opportune moment.<br /><br />There is still a Trojan horse, but the battle tactics and strategies of the adversaries are new and different in this version of the story. One thing the Trojans have left at their disposal in defense for this last battle is sand…en masse! So what do you do with all of it? You lure the opponents into it. That’s all I can say without giving it away. <br /><br />Well-loved heroes shine while others fall and just maybe, the Trojans will live on….<br /><br />***<br /><br />What a great read!<br /><br />This book had me dabble in some research on events, timelines, and characters. I knew I was on to something interesting as soon as I learned of this novel and am so happy my hunch on it was confirmed. <br /><br />As a lover of historical fiction and fantasy, I was eagerly anticipating the surprises in this novel. With my shield held at the ready as I began to read, <b>my armor proved to not hold up for very long and Kelly's narrative took to slaying my emotions in less than a quarter into the book.</b> I love it when that happens! What can I say? I'm a sucker for little ones, like young Diomedes and lil’ old ladies, though those were not in here.<br /><br />The blurb on the back of the book describes THE FALL OF THE PHOENIX<i>
  <b> "narrated with such close attention to the minute particulars of battle"</b>
</i> and I do agree with that. The scenes were certainly captivating and engrossing, but I also found it to be in balance with political intrigue and the characterization of the key players.<br /><br />While the first part of this novel shines by building up tension in the plot and characters with a few changes from the original, the latter takes home the cake as it capitalizes on the very cleverly injected turn of events drawing from other mythology and a decisive plan by the leaders of the respective factions. THIS was so unexpected and brilliant at the same time, it had me completely astonished. Nicely done!<br /><br />I definitely recommend this gem of a book to <b>ALL OF YOU!</b><br /><br />Enjoy :)<br /><br /><i>I received a physical copy of this novel from the author in exchange for an honest review. All opinions are my own. Thank you :)</i><br /><br />More of my reviews here:<br /><a href="https://scarlettreadzandrunz.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Through Novel Time &amp; Distance</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8217509092435498799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3498947465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3498947465" />
    <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence"><img alt="Mark Lawrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442536170p2/4508542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3498947465?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Lawrence" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence">Mark Lawrence</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3498947465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12320657517123922771">Daniel Kelly gave me a copy of the book at Bristolcon last year (2019), or more accurately: in the bar just outside Bristolcon which is where I'm to be found on Bristolcon day (though not this year as the event is cancelled).<br/><br/>He's a nice guy, so I read it.<br/><br/>I'm not sure what genre you'd call it. It's a re-imagining of the fall of Troy, but it's not a fantasy, there's no magic and no divine intervention. And you couldn't really call it historical fiction since it's based on myth rather than history.</span>
  <span id="freeText12320657517123922771" style="display:none">Daniel Kelly gave me a copy of the book at Bristolcon last year (2019), or more accurately: in the bar just outside Bristolcon which is where I'm to be found on Bristolcon day (though not this year as the event is cancelled).<br /><br />He's a nice guy, so I read it.<br /><br />I'm not sure what genre you'd call it. It's a re-imagining of the fall of Troy, but it's not a fantasy, there's no magic and no divine intervention. And you couldn't really call it historical fiction since it's based on myth rather than history. Perhaps mythological fiction, but the actual myth had gods and magic...<br /><br />Anyway. for the majority of the book the plot appears to stick fairly closely to the classical version. Achilles has his fight with Hector over the death of Patroclus (who is now a younger brother rather than an slightly older and very close friend). We see Agamemnon and Odysseus etc.<br /><br />The size of the armies are in line with the (to my mind somewhat dubious) Homeric claims, i.e around 200,000 for the Greeks. And we join the action in the 10th year of the siege.<br /><br />Kelly doesn't spend a lot of time making the setting feel 3000+ years ago, but the Greek legends are so bedded in our psyche that most of us come with the groundwork in place.<br /><br />There were times I had problems envisioning the scale of the place and how the Trojans ate for a decade under siege. The famous wooden horse for example is described as having its belly 50 feet off the ground. And later it's dragged in through the gates. I never figured out if the gates are stupendously tall or if they simply sealed a gap in the walls.<br /><br />To humanise the scale of the thing we see a lot of the story through the eyes of a "random" boy and we're plugged into his family drama. Our boy is, of course, sucked into the midst of things and soon gets to follow Achilles around.<br /><br />When the departure for the traditional story line occurs it's a fairly dramatic one - which is nice - though I did struggle with some of the motivations for the deviation.<br /><br />For me the main interest, rather than characters or world building was simply to see how the story would go/end. I feel this was probably the author's focus too as we shift from character to character following the main thread of the story and abandoning points of view when they leave focus.<br /><br />If you like swords and sandals fantasy without the fantasy, and take your wine in an amphora then you might want to beach your ship with the Greeks' thousand and watch Troy burn with Mr Kelly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12320657517123922771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2917442549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2917442549" />
    <a title="Eric Sparks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90611441-eric-sparks"><img alt="Eric Sparks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545111749p2/90611441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2917442549?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric Sparks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric Sparks" href="/user/show/90611441-eric-sparks">Eric Sparks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2917442549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2812795458847938574">Daniel’s historical fiction takes full advantage of its source material – both its strengths and weaknesses – to weave a tale from the final days of the mythic Trojan War. He captures the full grandeur of its heroes on both sides (Hector, Achilles, Priam, Agamemnon, Odysseus, and many others). Though a new telling, most of these famous characters feel true to personas we’ve associated with all of them. But he also takes advantage the conflicting source material to spurn some of the details (and </span>
  <span id="freeText2812795458847938574" style="display:none">Daniel’s historical fiction takes full advantage of its source material – both its strengths and weaknesses – to weave a tale from the final days of the mythic Trojan War. He captures the full grandeur of its heroes on both sides (Hector, Achilles, Priam, Agamemnon, Odysseus, and many others). Though a new telling, most of these famous characters feel true to personas we’ve associated with all of them. But he also takes advantage the conflicting source material to spurn some of the details (and timeline) to form another account, no less probable than any of the authoritative sources, and more in tune with the tastes of audiences in the modern West. Perhaps the greatest testament to the book is that you go in guarded against falling in love with the Trojan characters, knowing the fate the must befall at least most and likely all of them, but you find you can’t. The result is a sorrowful, yet uplifting, retelling of the Fall of Troy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2812795458847938574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2581299489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2581299489" />

<div id="review_2604649544" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2604649544" />
    <a title="Ken Stark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55335295-ken-stark"><img alt="Ken Stark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472703640p2/55335295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2604649544?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken Stark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken Stark" href="/user/show/55335295-ken-stark">Ken Stark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2604649544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14445488258539518883">The Fall of the Phoenix by Daniel Kelly gives us a look at the ancient city of Troy in a way in which we've never seen it before. We get to experience what daily life was like behind the walls, we sneak a peek at the machinations of the powerful and the would-be powerful, and we are granted a front row seat at some of the most epic battles in history. And though we know that it can't all end happily from the Trojans, it's the getting there that makes this book an exciting and entertaining read.<br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText14445488258539518883" style="display:none">The Fall of the Phoenix by Daniel Kelly gives us a look at the ancient city of Troy in a way in which we've never seen it before. We get to experience what daily life was like behind the walls, we sneak a peek at the machinations of the powerful and the would-be powerful, and we are granted a front row seat at some of the most epic battles in history. And though we know that it can't all end happily from the Trojans, it's the getting there that makes this book an exciting and entertaining read.<br /><br />The Fall of the Phoenix opens with the famous duel between Troy's favorite son, Hector, and the Greek hero, Achilles. Once friends, these two are now out for blood, and boy do they get it. Their epic fight is described in all of its gory detail, setting a wonderfully gruesome tone for the rest of the book. Daniel Kelly has clearly done his homework, and his clear, concise writing style can't help but draw the reader into the story. But this is no history lesson, nor is it a mere blow-by-blow accounting of the Trojans struggle for survival. This is tale of real people caught in an impossible situation, doing what they can and often what they must. It serves as a potent reminder that heroes and villains can come from the unlikeliest of places, and that the difference between the two is almost always a matter of perspective. Five enthusiastic stars for The Fall of the Phoenix and for Daniel Kelly. I can't wait to see where he'll take us next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14445488258539518883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3477552723" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3477552723" />
    <a title="Audrey S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10210054-audrey-s"><img alt="Audrey S" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563837679p2/10210054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3477552723?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Audrey S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Audrey S" href="/user/show/10210054-audrey-s">Audrey S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3477552723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14120228731227286011"><i> I received a free copy from the Author in exchange for my honest review </i><br/><br/>It really doesn’t matter how many times I read them, I’m always down for a mythology/historical fiction retelling 😂 There is just so much to examine and play around with that every story brings something new and I was very excited to see what new lens The Fall of the Phoenix would bring to the fall of Troy. <br/><br/>This novel does rely a little on the reader already knowing some of the story of Troy, but only so that it can flip it</span>
  <span id="freeText14120228731227286011" style="display:none"><i> I received a free copy from the Author in exchange for my honest review </i><br /><br />It really doesn’t matter how many times I read them, I’m always down for a mythology/historical fiction retelling 😂 There is just so much to examine and play around with that every story brings something new and I was very excited to see what new lens The Fall of the Phoenix would bring to the fall of Troy. <br /><br />This novel does rely a little on the reader already knowing some of the story of Troy, but only so that it can flip it on its head, and it is very fun to watch it play out. Kelly's writing shines in the small moments: the battle between Achilles and Hector (excellent!), the scene of the final reveal (no spoilers, but it’s good 😘), and the death of Priscus (which was hands down my favourite scene in the novel, it was so poignant, so full of emotion, and so freaking good; I would read the heck out of a book that followed the build up to that scene). <br /><br />The fairly large cast with POVs also allowed us to see many angles of the fall of Troy, however, this did feel like a weak point for such a short book, since it did leave the novel feeling just a little unfocused. <br /><br />With the ability to write scenes that hook you in, I can’t wait to see what Kelly does next, though I will be selfish and hope for more mythos 😁</span>
  <a data-text-id="14120228731227286011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2981193547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2981193547" />
    <a title="Xerxes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76908420-xerxes"><img alt="Xerxes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561471715p2/76908420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2981193547?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Xerxes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Xerxes" href="/user/show/76908420-xerxes">Xerxes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2981193547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer335864570218891783">This is a self-published novel that you MUST not miss. It has an alternate history, fantasy, heroic action, excellent attention to details of the fighting, city street combat. This is an epic journey to the city streets of Troy itself. I reviewed this book back in mid-2019. Now I feel this book needs that attention once again.<br/><br/>I loved the characters, the way Daniel has interpreted the novel, and it is clear he’s done his research. The plot of this novel is so good, that I will not spoil the twist</span>
  <span id="freeText335864570218891783" style="display:none">This is a self-published novel that you MUST not miss. It has an alternate history, fantasy, heroic action, excellent attention to details of the fighting, city street combat. This is an epic journey to the city streets of Troy itself. I reviewed this book back in mid-2019. Now I feel this book needs that attention once again.<br /><br />I loved the characters, the way Daniel has interpreted the novel, and it is clear he’s done his research. The plot of this novel is so good, that I will not spoil the twists or ending that come after this. The vivid descriptions of armor, battles. Everything about this novel is fantastic. This book had fantastic action sequences combined with a vivid sense of combat.<br /><br />This book has a better interpretation of the Iliad than what the movie depicts. The movie depicted the elite nobles of both sides, Trojan and Greek scheming against each other. When in reality, this really wasn’t the case at all? Both sides knew each other pretty well. Daniel must have scoured through the annals of Greek literature to find some obscure references of which I am sure he will have added into this novel. Where they showed all the elites of both sides, Trojan and Greek scheming against each other when in reality the Trojans and the Greek nobility knew each other. Daniel must have read some obscure material and used it for this book. Diomedes was my favorite character in this book. I liked his innocence, because that war, whether it happened, took a toll on everybody. I imagine that was what the aftermath of WW2 was. Priam was excellent, and Agamemnon, he was a cunning old wolf. Odysseus is older than I interpreted. You also got to see the viewpoint of the Trojans, which is very rare. Also, search Assassin’s Creed Odyssey Ambient Music for 4 hours. This is perfect for the ambiance and immersion.<br /><br />The dialogue, the prose, everything about this book is excellent. I’m in praise. What more can I say? I would have wanted this novel to be bigger, and more explanations as I have a lot of questions regarding this book. This could be an under-explored genre that, if Daniel capitalizes on, could work very well for him.<br /><br />Thank you so much for writing this, Daniel. This is historical fantasy at its best.<br /><br />This is a self-published novel that you MUST not miss. It has an alternate history, fantasy, heroic action, excellent attention to details of the fighting, city street combat. This is an epic journey to the city streets of Troy itself. I reviewed this book back in mid-2019. Now I feel this book needs that attention once again.<br /><br />I loved the characters, the way Daniel has interpreted the novel, and it is clear he’s done his research. The plot of this novel is so good, that I will not spoil the twists or ending that come after this. The vivid descriptions of armor, battles. Everything about this novel is fantastic. This book had fantastic action sequences combined with a vivid sense of combat.<br /><br />This book has a better interpretation of the Iliad than what the movie depicts. The movie depicted the elite nobles of both sides, Trojan and Greek scheming against each other. When in reality, this really wasn’t the case at all? Both sides knew each other pretty well. Daniel must have scoured through the annals of Greek literature to find some obscure references of which I am sure he will have added into this novel. Where they showed all the elites of both sides, Trojan and Greek scheming against each other when in reality the Trojans and the Greek nobility knew each other. Daniel must have read some obscure material and used it for this book. Diomedes was my favorite character in this book. I liked his innocence, because that war, whether it happened, took a toll on everybody. I imagine that was what the aftermath of WW2 was. Priam was excellent, and Agamemnon, he was a cunning old wolf. Odysseus is older than I interpreted. You also got to see the viewpoint of the Trojans, which is very rare. Also, search Assassin’s Creed Odyssey Ambient Music for 4 hours. This is perfect for the ambiance and immersion.<br /><br />The dialogue, the prose, everything about this book is excellent. I’m in praise. What more can I say? I would have wanted this novel to be bigger, and more explanations as I have a lot of questions regarding this book. This could be an under-explored genre that, if Daniel capitalizes on, could work very well for him.<br /><br />Thank you so much for writing this, Daniel. This is historical fantasy at its best. 10/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="335864570218891783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3248983064" />
    <a title="Tom Lloyd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1315922-tom-lloyd"><img alt="Tom Lloyd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512750257p2/1315922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3248983064?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Lloyd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Lloyd" href="/user/show/1315922-tom-lloyd">Tom Lloyd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3248983064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7205603131387703940">Full disclosure - the author gave me a free copy of the book, but having said that I wouldn't have reviewed it unless I'd enjoyed it.( Or I'd really hated it to the point that keeping quiet would have annoyed me, I suppose.) <br/><br/>Fortunately, the former was true. This is a hugely entertaining slice of historical fiction, drawing on historical source with a little tweaking to make it work better as fiction. It's a debut novel (so far as I'm aware) and there's a little roughness especially at the start</span>
  <span id="freeText7205603131387703940" style="display:none">Full disclosure - the author gave me a free copy of the book, but having said that I wouldn't have reviewed it unless I'd enjoyed it.( Or I'd really hated it to the point that keeping quiet would have annoyed me, I suppose.) <br /><br />Fortunately, the former was true. This is a hugely entertaining slice of historical fiction, drawing on historical source with a little tweaking to make it work better as fiction. It's a debut novel (so far as I'm aware) and there's a little roughness especially at the start, but VERY few debuts are perfectly polished. Quickly it settles into an absorbing slice of history with normal, flawed people living through legendary times, furious action and tragic heroism. He doesn't dwell upon the violence, but nor does he shy from the reality and to me it seemed an honest portrayal of how battle would be viewed by ancient warriors. Highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7205603131387703940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12036192834223857475">The Fall of the Phoenix by Daniel Kelly is a mesmerizing novel as it takes you through the final battle of the famous city of Troy. Kelly brings the characters live as they face fears beyond our wildest dreams. Men fighting demigods, mythology at its best. It is hard to pick a favorite character as their roles of good and evil alternate, or it kills them off. I loved the mystique and grandeur of the novel as Kelly plants a visual picture of events. <br/> <br/>Daniel Kelly has the gift of adding energetic </span>
  <span id="freeText12036192834223857475" style="display:none">The Fall of the Phoenix by Daniel Kelly is a mesmerizing novel as it takes you through the final battle of the famous city of Troy. Kelly brings the characters live as they face fears beyond our wildest dreams. Men fighting demigods, mythology at its best. It is hard to pick a favorite character as their roles of good and evil alternate, or it kills them off. I loved the mystique and grandeur of the novel as Kelly plants a visual picture of events. <br /> <br />Daniel Kelly has the gift of adding energetic battles that makes The Fall of the Phoenix feel as if it really happened this way. The characters are bigger than life and accomplish amazing feats or die trying. During a time when offenses were fought to the death by sword or arrow, this novel has you experience the suffering and glory within the gates of this great city until its use is drained dry.   <br /></span>

<div id="review_3238829042" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3238829042" />
    <a title="Bohdana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19461330-bohdana"><img alt="Bohdana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568856679p2/19461330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3238829042?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bohdana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bohdana" href="/user/show/19461330-bohdana">Bohdana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Bronze Age society, action, adventure</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19461330-bohdana?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19461330-bohdana?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3238829042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17224350037083915593">Well, I didn't expect that. <br/><br/>There was plenty of action, it's fast-paced, plenty of attention to various characters, and it's also something to read for the atmosphere. There are scenes that we don't get to see in <i>The Iliad</i> (like the 'Trojan horse') and it gave the characters more attention, which was great to read. There is plenty of action. It's something to read if you've read <i>The Iliad</i> and <i>Odyssey</i>, it takes a more historical approach to the events (that's to say there was no direct godly inte</span>
  <span id="freeText17224350037083915593" style="display:none">Well, I didn't expect that. <br /><br />There was plenty of action, it's fast-paced, plenty of attention to various characters, and it's also something to read for the atmosphere. There are scenes that we don't get to see in <i>The Iliad</i> (like the 'Trojan horse') and it gave the characters more attention, which was great to read. There is plenty of action. It's something to read if you've read <i>The Iliad</i> and <i>Odyssey</i>, it takes a more historical approach to the events (that's to say there was no direct godly intervention). Also, those salty over the events of <i>The Iliad</i> should read the entire thing. Like the material it builds on, the book has a lot of characters which might be a bit intimidating to those who haven't read <i>The Iliad</i> but if someone is used to reading books with many characters, I think they could still keep track of events (just be ready for it when reading the book). Those that love war or siege stories will like this. <br /><br />-----small Edit: I was looking over my book log and found a good quote I noted: <br /><br />-----<i>"War makes butchers of all good men, Achilles."</i> (pg 59). <br /><br />Those that like stories to be concise might not like this. We get to see what the characters are thinking but there might be more words used to describe it than necessary (the book is short so maybe there is that...). <br /><br />The language in the book is very formal at times (reminds me of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49522119.Rise_of_the_Phoenix__A_Tale_of_Hayara___1_" title="Rise of the Phoenix (A Tale of Hayara, #1) by T. Isajanyan" rel="nofollow noopener">Rise of the Phoenix</a> in that respect) more than some high fantasy I've been reading lately. It definitely adds to the atmosphere. It might take some getting used to when reading it. The characters still are very human which helps to get used to the formal language.<br /><br />There was something about the society that wasn't explained much (probably to avoid info-dumping for no reason):<br />- Greeks don't bow (<i>proskynesis</i>) unless it's to a god(s). The Persians did bow (the Ancient Near East had the practice) so it's one thing for Trojans or Greeks who encounter or entertain those from Asia Minor.<br />- The wine was usually mixed (not diluting it was seen as 'barbaric'). There were specific mixing bowls (kraters) for that.<br />That's it for the fun facts but mostly it's just the stuff that was ever-present that didn't really need mentioning but I figured to mention for the enthusiasts.<br /><br />Overall, it's a good book. <br /><br />***I received a review copy from the author through Voracious Readers***</span>
  <a data-text-id="17224350037083915593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Tara Phillips" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42013730-tara-phillips"><img alt="Tara Phillips" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2970198881?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tara Phillips" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tara Phillips" href="/user/show/42013730-tara-phillips">Tara Phillips</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2970198881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12469712167627764749">Opening prolong scene captured my attention with bold imagery. Bodyguards by the dozens shielded with heavy battle armor. The army pointed straight at our protagonist; Hector. The timing; final days of the Trojan War in the city of Troy. Hector is he good or bad? The scene suggests he’s angered someone in the prince castle but time will tell. <br/>I read the book and have my interpretation of bad with good intentions and good with bad action. Meaning his will might be correct but in his responsibilit</span>
  <span id="freeText12469712167627764749" style="display:none">Opening prolong scene captured my attention with bold imagery. Bodyguards by the dozens shielded with heavy battle armor. The army pointed straight at our protagonist; Hector. The timing; final days of the Trojan War in the city of Troy. Hector is he good or bad? The scene suggests he’s angered someone in the prince castle but time will tell. <br />I read the book and have my interpretation of bad with good intentions and good with bad action. Meaning his will might be correct but in his responsibility and job his morals are set aside and for that evil emerges. <br /><br />Master storytelling reveals Homer questioning what if the war never happened. How would lives be changed? <br />If the Greek armies took different battle strategies? What if?<br />Main elements of this Greek marvel; Battles, conflict, time, culture, and circumstance. I felt drawn to Homer imagining him to have wisdom that he doesn’t quite ever credit for.<br />But today is today and the Greek’s govern over the city of Troy. Chilling descriptions with accuracy to mysteries surrounding mythology and history as the plot reads as real life. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12469712167627764749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

    <a title="Shreyas Adhikari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67002454-shreyas-adhikari"><img alt="Shreyas Adhikari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492839389p2/67002454.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3037898903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14096279398309493305">Alright, first of all let me thank Daniel for reintroducing me to the magnificent, blood soaked world of Greek mythology again. I fell in love with the characters of Achilles, Hector and Priam (surprisingly, the old man struck me as a whining, doddering fool in earlier versions and the Iliad.) They are flawed mortals, not demigods, each with his own dreams, ambitions, frustrations and weaknesses. And yet each has the capacity for apotheosis:- transcendence to godhood through one's actions. <br/><br/>The b</span>
  <span id="freeText14096279398309493305" style="display:none">Alright, first of all let me thank Daniel for reintroducing me to the magnificent, blood soaked world of Greek mythology again. I fell in love with the characters of Achilles, Hector and Priam (surprisingly, the old man struck me as a whining, doddering fool in earlier versions and the Iliad.) They are flawed mortals, not demigods, each with his own dreams, ambitions, frustrations and weaknesses. And yet each has the capacity for apotheosis:- transcendence to godhood through one's actions. <br /><br />The battle sequences are visceral and satisfy every lover of grimdark. I never realized the glory and gore of a siege can transform into tightly-knit, brutal street fighting within hours. Claustrophobic, unholy and awful. And yet Daniel manages to spill blood in a heroic way, narrowing down the narrative to fit in the perspectives of every prominent character engaged in the bitter tussle. Wonderfully written, well researched and with a pleasant surprise towards the end, The Fall of the Phoenix deserves a read. And a re-read, of course.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14096279398309493305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2930451941?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2930451941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10950694467274812232">The Fall of the Phoenix by Daniel Kelly is a detailed retelling of the fantastic battle of Troy. The prologue was wonderfully gritty, detailing a battle between Achilles and Hector. The depth of attention paid to every single aspect of this battle sets the tone for an informative and great story. The city of Troy is fully explored, exposing nuances and everyday life that is seldom written about. This book is a great combination of history and mythology as the author explores the history of the t</span>
  <span id="freeText10950694467274812232" style="display:none">The Fall of the Phoenix by Daniel Kelly is a detailed retelling of the fantastic battle of Troy. The prologue was wonderfully gritty, detailing a battle between Achilles and Hector. The depth of attention paid to every single aspect of this battle sets the tone for an informative and great story. The city of Troy is fully explored, exposing nuances and everyday life that is seldom written about. This book is a great combination of history and mythology as the author explores the history of the time. Not merely just a recounting of history, this tale tells of the struggles for survival in a very unique time. Often it's hard to discern who to root for, who is the bad or the good guy, but knowing that everyone involved has their own unique motivations and cultural influences. The battles scenes are so spot on, you feel you are a witness to the heroics displayed. Fine writing sets this book apart from simple historical fiction. Highly recommend. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10950694467274812232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3416550238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3416550238" />
    <a title="M.T. Ceres" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/103418602-m-t-ceres"><img alt="M.T. Ceres" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581411768p2/103418602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3416550238?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M.T. Ceres" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M.T. Ceres" href="/user/show/103418602-m-t-ceres">M.T. Ceres</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3416550238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6267731126217287054">Brilliant read and well worth five stars.<br/><br/>I romped quite quickly to Chapter Three, because at the end of Chapter One the story took off and I had engaged with the characters, who were very well rounded. By Chapter three I had become familiar with the names of the characters and who was on what side. Additionally, I had settled in to the author's narrative style.<br/>The Author's style suits the genre and focus of this story perfectly. The style is masculine and precise. It is really sympathetic to the</span>
  <span id="freeText6267731126217287054" style="display:none">Brilliant read and well worth five stars.<br /><br />I romped quite quickly to Chapter Three, because at the end of Chapter One the story took off and I had engaged with the characters, who were very well rounded. By Chapter three I had become familiar with the names of the characters and who was on what side. Additionally, I had settled in to the author's narrative style.<br />The Author's style suits the genre and focus of this story perfectly. The style is masculine and precise. It is really sympathetic to the military focus of The Fall of the Phoenix. Kelly knows his history and knows how to set a scene with historical accuracy and attention to detail.<br /><br />By the time I got to Chapter Six I was completely invested in the story, the characters and the outcome. <br />The relationship between Achilles and Diomedes was, as intimated earlier in the work, beautifully developed, and was one of the key points of interest in the story for me. I would have loved to have read Diomedes back story in the prologue.<br />Enjoyed the portrayal of Achilles as a man and a warrior-god, it was interesting to see the juxtaposition that the author presented, it was handled really well and humanised a character from history, who is usually presented as a god. The villain Agamemnon was dastardly, but in the end un-stoppable, even though he got exactly what he deserved. <br /><br />No spoliers, but the end of Chapter Fifteen got me totally in 'The Feels'. Following this the build up to the climatic ending was masterfully paced. <br />I could feel my own adrenaline building alongside the action, and this is the point where, I couldn't put the story down. It felt like I was there. <br />This is why I gave The Fall of the Phoenix five stars, because of how the progression of the tale was handled, in terms of reader engagement. Really gentle build up, not too much information at first, as the characters were introduced and dynamics were set. <br />Then, it felt like a 'stepping in' to another reality which in my opinion good fantasy should be. There comes a point in the tale, when we have arrived fully in this other world, and are immersed in the milieu, our disbelief is suspended and we are there! We care about the society and what happens to the people.<br /><br />A fantastic written city battle. The attention to strategic position and the historical accuracy of the means of defence was masterful. The final moments and the fall of Troy was so perfectly wrought, I felt the loss, it was very poignant.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6267731126217287054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3154634126276598732">Long long ago... OK in 2004... the movie Troy was released. I was in college and my buddy and I decided to go see it one Saturday afternoon. It was a glorious day, and we hoped it would be a brilliant film.<br/><br/>Alas, we thought it was terrible (apologies if you liked it). After what seemed like an eternity I turned to my friend and said "when are they going to show us the bloody horse?"<br/><br/>Eventually, the movie was over, upon leaving the cinema, we were blinded by the sunlight - our endurance had been se</span>
  <span id="freeText3154634126276598732" style="display:none">Long long ago... OK in 2004... the movie Troy was released. I was in college and my buddy and I decided to go see it one Saturday afternoon. It was a glorious day, and we hoped it would be a brilliant film.<br /><br />Alas, we thought it was terrible (apologies if you liked it). After what seemed like an eternity I turned to my friend and said "when are they going to show us the bloody horse?"<br /><br />Eventually, the movie was over, upon leaving the cinema, we were blinded by the sunlight - our endurance had been severely tested. We went to the pub to meet friends, it felt like we hadn't seen them for years, not hours (this film is a tad over three hours long by the way, and it felt every minute of it) - of course, there is only one GIF that really sums it up.<br /><br />If I had been inclined to read The Iliad before seeing the film, I certainly wasn't after. <br /><br />Anyway - all of this preamble leads us to The Fall of  the Phoenix by Daniel Kelly. After hearing of the book online it peaked my interest, mainly because it appeared like it could be a slightly different take on the old story. The reviews online were also incredibly solid, so when the author offered to gift me a copy I jumped at the chance.<br /><br />The Fall of the Phoenix starts strong and continues in the same fashion throughout. We open with a face of between one time friends Hector and Achilles - the strongest fighters of their day. The story takes place over a period of time between this fight and the fall of Troy. Most people will be familiar with how Troy falls in the end (see horse above), but the author takes a different view point on the final events leading to Troy's destruction. <br /><br /><br />We spend most of our time flitting between characters in the besieged Troy and the camp of the invading army. On the side of the Trojans the story story is built on what the soldiers can do to stop the siege. Our invaders want a similar outcome, but obviously in a different way. The siege has lasted ten years already, they want it to end so they can fill their pockets and go home. Achilles, who is most reluctantly fighting on the side of Greece, features prominently throughout. Despite myself I couldn't stop picturing Brad Pitt - but aside from that the author did a great job in portraying this alleged demigod. <br /><br />Not just to pick out Achilles - the author has written each character brilliantly and brought them to life in new ways. <br /><br />The author has written an excellent take on a familiar story. This is Troy as you have never seen it before. It is a great read and one which I would highly recommend to anyone. Get on it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3154634126276598732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3269423252" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3269423252" />
    <a title="A.M. Steiner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5458820-a-m-steiner"><img alt="A.M. Steiner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489418565p2/5458820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3269423252?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.M. Steiner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.M. Steiner" href="/user/show/5458820-a-m-steiner">A.M. Steiner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3269423252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16991354287017212304">A muscular retelling of the fall of Troy, but not as you know it!<br/><br/>It's a brave author who seeks to re-invent the Illiad (or more accurately, the lost Aethiopis of the Epic cycle). Not only does it invite direct comparison with Homer, but also some spectacularly successful recent attempts, most notably The Song of Achilles by Madeline Miller. <br/><br/>Fortunately, Daniel Kelly proves up to the task with this finely written action-orientated interpretation. The focus is very much on the male warriors who do</span>
  <span id="freeText16991354287017212304" style="display:none">A muscular retelling of the fall of Troy, but not as you know it!<br /><br />It's a brave author who seeks to re-invent the Illiad (or more accurately, the lost Aethiopis of the Epic cycle). Not only does it invite direct comparison with Homer, but also some spectacularly successful recent attempts, most notably The Song of Achilles by Madeline Miller. <br /><br />Fortunately, Daniel Kelly proves up to the task with this finely written action-orientated interpretation. The focus is very much on the male warriors who dominate the original texts, but there's also a keen eye on the human cost of war - and the motif of the fallen soldier. The sense of place is excellent and the characters are well developed and believable, in particular the youth Diomedes. <br /><br />I wouldn't necessarily class this as fantasy, more as psuedo-historical fiction. While the gods and omens are present in the minds of the characters, there is nothing fantastical on the page. If anything this reads like a 'truth behind the legend' exposé.<br /><br />It's not until the latter stages of the book that the story diverges significantly from versions you might have read before. For my taste, this was actually where it was at its strongest, and the unexpected finale left me looking forward to the next installment. I read somewhere that Kelly is also considering applying the same treatment to the Ulster Cycle. I sincerely hope he does, as I expect the result would be spectacular.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16991354287017212304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3043696720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3043696720" />
    <a title="High Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/105213418-high-light"><img alt="High Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573390882p2/105213418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3043696720?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Light" href="/user/show/105213418-high-light">High Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3043696720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3023363346153696939">If you are looking for a fine, well-crafted retelling of classical Greece’s war with the Trojans then look no further than this! Author Daniel Kelly has proven himself to be a master storyteller who takes a well-known storyline from antiquity and gives it his own spin which I could not help but marvel at. This begins with a duel between two of ancient Greece’s greatest heroes: one being the Trojan warrior, Hector and the other being Greece’s Achilles. It goes on until Achilles ends up killing He</span>
  <span id="freeText3023363346153696939" style="display:none">If you are looking for a fine, well-crafted retelling of classical Greece’s war with the Trojans then look no further than this! Author Daniel Kelly has proven himself to be a master storyteller who takes a well-known storyline from antiquity and gives it his own spin which I could not help but marvel at. This begins with a duel between two of ancient Greece’s greatest heroes: one being the Trojan warrior, Hector and the other being Greece’s Achilles. It goes on until Achilles ends up killing Hector by tiring him while in battle. I am one who is not really a fan of violence and gore so I had to force myself to read through this novel which is laden with that kind of stuff. But I won’t lie though, I still felt riveted to this story because the action goes on from the first page until the last. And you will find yourself agreeing with me that Kelly does so well with explaining certain changes he’s made to the classic story you will want to read other books by him if he has any. This is a work of historical fiction and it helped that I had some knowledge of the Trojan War before I got to read this book.<br /><br />The book is all violence right from start to end. There is endless mention of blood, wounds, sores, weapons, and the sort. There are also some episodes of bromance in this story between Achilles and a character called Diomedes and again Achilles and a surprise character you will come upon in the middle of the book. Oh! And there are loads of surprises for you. I mentioned before that this is a retelling and Kelly is a master at it. The ending will leave you feeling amused and satisfied that you chose to read this interesting book. There is a lack of women characters in this story as mainly it is about soldiers at war with each other. If you are not familiar with the Trojan War then I suggest to you to do your research online because you may need it to understand the story better. Does this story include gods and goddesses? I’ll let you find that out for yourself! Does this story have a vengeful god or goddess who is helping one side win over the other? Again, I’ll let you find that out for yourself.<br /><br />This book is for the Greek mythology enthusiasts. I learned about this story from back in elementary and high school. I think I haven’t seen a movie made out of it or? I don’t know. But yeah, this book is not for the faint of heart as it is a blood and gore fest. This book is for the lover of war stories. This book is for one who loves a fine and innovative retelling of one of history’s greatest wars. Before you have any doubts about this book, I assure you that it will make you so satisfied to have read it, especially when you are familiar with the famous men of old, Achilles and Hector.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3023363346153696939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3442911265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3442911265" />
    <a title="Hannah Brunsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39676257-hannah-brunsden"><img alt="Hannah Brunsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603539091p2/39676257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3442911265?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Brunsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Brunsden" href="/user/show/39676257-hannah-brunsden">Hannah Brunsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3442911265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3915114281755325490"><br/>Okay so let me start off my saying I LOVE greek mythology, it’s always been a topic area that I easily get drawn into and love to read about! I find the brutality of the gods and heroes fascinating in this ever evolving Greek world. <br/><br/>I have read about the battle of Troy before but Kelly’s version was really refreshing to me, I found the writing style very informative but still enjoyable to read, it flowed easily from one place to the other while still giving me my fix of facts that I always want </span>
  <span id="freeText3915114281755325490" style="display:none"><br />Okay so let me start off my saying I LOVE greek mythology, it’s always been a topic area that I easily get drawn into and love to read about! I find the brutality of the gods and heroes fascinating in this ever evolving Greek world. <br /><br />I have read about the battle of Troy before but Kelly’s version was really refreshing to me, I found the writing style very informative but still enjoyable to read, it flowed easily from one place to the other while still giving me my fix of facts that I always want when reading mythology work!<br /><br />All in all I loved this book and it was the perfect mythology fix that I was needing, I feel the true testament of how good this book was for me is the fact that even though I knew how the story ended and that there are certain characters I shouldn’t get attached to because of their fates I still did. Kelly’s writing was able to overcome what I knew and made me continually want to read a story I’ve already read a number of times from different sources!<br /><br />Recommend this to anyone who loves Greek mythology and wants a refreshing versions of the battle of Troy and the Trojan war!<br />•<br />✨𝘋𝘪𝘴𝘤𝘭𝘢𝘪𝘮𝘦𝘳: 𝘐 𝘸𝘢𝘴 𝘴𝘦𝘯𝘵 𝘢 𝘤𝘰𝘱𝘺 𝘰𝘧 𝘵𝘩𝘪𝘴 𝘣𝘰𝘰𝘬 𝘣𝘺 𝘵𝘩𝘦 𝘢𝘶𝘵𝘩𝘰𝘳, 𝘩𝘰𝘸𝘦𝘷𝘦𝘳 𝘳𝘦𝘨𝘢𝘳𝘥𝘭𝘦𝘴𝘴 𝘰𝘧 𝘵𝘩𝘢𝘵 𝘵𝘩𝘪𝘴 𝘪𝘴 𝘴𝘵𝘪𝘭𝘭 𝘢𝘯 𝘩𝘰𝘯𝘦𝘴𝘵 𝘳𝘦𝘷𝘪𝘦𝘸!✨</span>
  <a data-text-id="3915114281755325490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rJ6BxZvYtrxnMXYD98XdUETSv9RxkT4XO7LGtH1387iWuOgXIIZ/1MAawmIAMNePko1YHL8csHBgzIAFsDQBIg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UOw2nDSet0qQNGMx7G/Bk+FSsfgIS/iDYt2QqQy+6Llqyl9Oj8B+Ijcf11AbmstMNw1WMMbGduQ5o9YYwf0aIw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8163685702008070622">Irish Author. Born in Donegal on the northern edge of the wild Atlantic way. If you have never been, I highly recommend that you visit and you will see exactly why I love history. Great teachers and a love of good historical fiction authors broadened my love of ancient history to a worldwide level. I would love to have a go at writing some of our own amazing Irish legends one day. </span>
